Root cause was in `app.jsx`: when `/api/history` returned a non-empty array (the DEMO_MODE default), it overwrote `window.GTM.proposals` with sparse history-derived entries — silently discarding all four curated `data.js` seeds (Banyan Health, Verdant Logistics, Arcadia Insurance, Thornfield Foods). Two fixes applied:
- **Seed preservation**: stash the original data.js proposals into `window.GTM._seedProposals` on first load so the curated entries survive subsequent `/api/history` refreshes. Merge history-derived entries with seeds, history winning by id (real run state takes priority), unmatched seeds appended.
- **Real company names from metadata**: read `metadata.client_name` first (the data IS already in the history fixture), then fall back to a `humanizeSlug()` helper that converts `harbor-property-mgmt` → `Harbor Property Mgmt`. Production history records that ship without `client_name` won't display kebab slugs anymore.

The verb "play" promised a behavior the app didn't deliver; the operator had no way to tell the cursor wasn't actually advancing.

Real playback now:
- **`playbackIndex` state**: tracks the currently-playing transcript line. `data-playing="true"` is set on that line in the DOM.
- **Tick interval** (700ms): while `playing === true`, advances `playbackIndex`. Auto-stops when reaching the last line and flips `playing` back to false so the icon is honest about the end-of-transcript state.
- **`startOrPausePlayback()`** handler: toggles `playing` and seeds `playbackIndex` to 0 on first start (so a fresh play begins at the top, not from -1).
- **Reset on call switch**: `useEffect([activeId])` clears both `playing` and `playbackIndex` so the cursor doesn't leak into a different transcript.
- **Auto-scroll**: the active line's `ref` calls `scrollIntoView({ block: 'nearest', behavior: 'smooth' })` so the playing line stays visible without yanking the user.
- **CSS highlight**: `[data-playing="true"]` gets a tinted background, accent left-border, and a subtle outline so the eye locks onto the cursor at a glance.

Added Playwright test: clicks Play, asserts a line gains `data-playing="true"` within one tick, waits another tick and confirms the active line's aria-label CHANGED (proves real advancement, not a static highlight), pauses and confirms the same line stays marked (proves the interval was cleared), switches calls via AppContext and confirms playback resets to zero playing lines. `bun run typecheck` clean, 3 calls tests green.

=== claude  2026-05-05T14:56:10.739Z  session 170db5f4 MATCH ===

Twenty-ninth defect closed — three intertwined bugs in the agent playground per-tuning path:

1. **Sticky configError** — when a previous agent's config fetch failed, `configError` state never cleared on agent switch (effect only ever *set* on cache hit, never reset). Switching to a clean agent kept the prior error message displayed against the new agent's id. Fixed by always syncing `configError` to the current agent's cache state.

2. **Mount-swapping fallback stranded the ref** — old render path `if (configError) return <different-div>` replaced the entire convai-mount. Once the error cleared on agent switch, the next render put the convai-mount back, but the create-effect didn't re-run (deps were stable). The mount sat empty forever. Fixed by rendering the error as a *sibling overlay* via a new `.convai-host` wrapper, leaving the mount alive at all times.

3. **React reconciliation race** — even with the above fixed, prop-change updates left the create-effect's append racing with cleanup, leaving `.convai-mount` empty. Fixed by keying ConvaiWidget on `active.key` at the playground site, forcing a clean remount per agent.

=== claude  2026-05-06T08:03:58.782Z  session 170db5f4 MATCH ===
[assistant] **Cron iteration 14 — 1 real security finding shipped:**

- gtm_ops #92: server.js was calling `app.listen(port)` with no host arg → bound to `0.0.0.0` (all interfaces). Combined with `/api/restart` and other unprotected POST routes (`/api/users/:id/role`, `/api/audit-logs/cleanup`, `/api/workspace/:id/invite`, `/api/gdpr/delete` — all sans auth), the dev box was trivially abusable from anywhere on the LAN. Now defaults to `127.0.0.1`; override with `HOST=0.0.0.0` for genuine container deployments. Loud startup warning if non-loopback explicitly chosen.

**Real exposure found, capped.** RBAC on the POST routes themselves is a bigger refactor (~20 sites) — tracked as follow-up.

**Total: 32 PRs.**

Going idle.

I tried to provision DNS automatically. My wrangler-OAuth token has `pages:write` and `zone:read`, but Cloudflare denies it on the DNS-records endpoint, and it can't create scoped API tokens either. So there are two manual one-time clicks I cannot do for you. Plain English:

**What you need to do (one minute):**

1. **Add ONE DNS record** so `app.wranngle.com` resolves.
   - Open Cloudflare dashboard → `wranngle.com` zone → **DNS** → **Add record**
   - Type: `CNAME`, Name: `app`, Target: `gtm-ops.pages.dev`, Proxied: **on**, TTL: Auto
   - Save. Wait ~30 seconds. `app.wranngle.com` will start serving.

2. **Add ONE GitHub secret** so the new auto-deploy workflow can run.
   - Go to https://dash.cloudflare.com/profile/api-tokens → **Create Token** → use the **"Edit Cloudflare Workers"** template → **Continue → Create Token** → copy the value
   - Go to https://github.com/wranngle/gtm_ops/settings/secrets/actions → **New repository secret** → Name `CLOUDFLARE_API_TOKEN`, value = the token you just copied → Save
   - Then merge PR #139.

After those two clicks, future merges to `main` deploy automatically and `app.wranngle.com` is the canonical console host. No more "I asked for X, did it ship" mystery — the workflow makes it visible per-merge.

=== claude  2026-05-07T01:35:20.512Z  session 0510ed4a MATCH ===
[assistant] This is DNS negative caching, not a deploy problem.

The Cloudflare side is fully live: Google DNS (`8.8.8.8`) returns the right anycast IPs (`104.21.37.156`, `172.67.210.82`) and a direct fetch with `--resolve` returns `301 → /console/`.

The problem: **your local resolver cached NXDOMAIN before the CNAME existed.** Any resolver that asked "does `app.wranngle.com` exist?" before you added the record got back "no" — and that "no" is cached for the SOA's negative-cache TTL (1800 seconds / 30 min on the wranngle.com zone). Even though the record now exists, your machine and browser will keep saying "doesn't exist" until that cache expires.

Three ways to bypass it right now:

1. **Open in a different browser** that uses DNS-over-HTTPS to a fresh resolver (Chrome Settings → Privacy → "Use secure DNS" → Cloudflare or Google). DoH bypasses your OS resolver entirely.
2. **Flush local caches:** `ipconfig /flushdns` in a Windows cmd / PowerShell (since you're on WSL), then in Chrome go to `chrome://net-internals/#dns` → Clear host cache.
3. **Try on your phone over cellular** (separate resolver, hasn't seen the NXDOMAIN).

Or just wait ~25 more minutes from when you added the CNAME and refresh.

I'll keep watching the auto-merge. Once PR #139 lands, the deploy-pages workflow runs once on main as a fresh redeploy — purely confirming, no functional change. Nothing else for you to do.

1. First effect: load script.
2. Second effect: agent_id sync + listener.
3. Third effect: useEffect[agent_id, ready, ...] creates `el`, sets `widgetRef.current = el`.

- L429-441: `[ctx, effectiveTextOnly]` effect — sets dynamic-variables, override-config

- Initial render: ready=false. Mount effect skipped (because `if (!agent_id || !ready) return undefined`). ctx effect runs but `widgetRef.current` is null → returns.
- Polling fires setReady(true). Re-render.
